</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2011 England riots</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_anti-austerity_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 United Kingdom anti-austerity protests">2011 United Kingdom anti-austerity protests</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em;width: 300px">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 125%; background-color: #CEE0F2; vertical-align: middle">2011 England riots</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa"><a href="/wiki/File:Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Carpetright store after Tottenham riots.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg/300px-Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg" width="300" height="225" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg/450px-Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg/600px-Carpetright_store_after_Tottenham_riots.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div>Firefighters douse a shop and flats destroyed by arson during the initial rioting in <a href="/wiki/Tottenham" title="Tottenham">Tottenham</a>, London</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Date</th>
<td>6–11 August 2011 (although incidents continued after this period)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Location</th>
<td><span class="location">Several districts of <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, and several other areas<sup id="cite_ref-guardianmap_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianmap-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraphmap_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphmap-2">[2]</a></sup></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Causes</th>
<td>Escalation of events following fatal police shooting of Mark Duggan</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Methods</th>
<td>Rioting, <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looting</a>, arson, <a href="/wiki/Robbery" title="Robbery">mugging</a>, assault, murder</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #CEE0F2; vertical-align: middle">Reported fatalities and injuries</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">5 deaths<sup id="cite_ref-death_one_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_one-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-death_two_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_two-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smh_leeds_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smh_leeds-5">[5]</a></sup><br />
16+ members of public injured<sup id="cite_ref-independent_injuries_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_injuries-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_mugging_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_mugging-7">[7]</a></sup><br />
186 police officers, 3 <a href="/wiki/Police_community_support_officer" title="Police community support officer">police community support officers</a><sup id="cite_ref-pcs.org.uk_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcs.org.uk-8">[8]</a></sup> as well as five police dogs injured<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_figures_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_figures-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Between 6 and 11 August 2011, thousands of people rioted in several <a href="/wiki/London_boroughs" title="London boroughs">London boroughs</a> and in cities and towns across <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. The resulting chaos generated <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looting</a>, arson, and mass deployment of police and resulted in the death of five people. Disturbances began on 6 August after a protest in <a href="/wiki/Tottenham" title="Tottenham">Tottenham</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Mark_Duggan" title="Death of Mark Duggan">death of Mark Duggan</a>, a local man who was shot dead by police on 4 August.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Several violent clashes with police ensued, along with the destruction of police vehicles, a <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker bus</a>, and many homes and businesses, thus rapidly gaining attention from the media. Overnight, looting took place in <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hale" title="Tottenham Hale">Tottenham Hale</a> retail park and nearby <a href="/wiki/Wood_Green" title="Wood Green">Wood Green</a>. The following days saw similar scenes in other parts of London, with the most rioting taking place in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hackney" title="London Borough of Hackney">Hackney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brixton" title="Brixton">Brixton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walthamstow" title="Walthamstow">Walthamstow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peckham" title="Peckham">Peckham</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Enfield" title="London Borough of Enfield">Enfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battersea" title="Battersea">Battersea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ealing" title="Ealing">Ealing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barking" title="Barking">Barking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woolwich" title="Woolwich">Woolwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewisham" title="Lewisham">Lewisham</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Ham" title="East Ham">East Ham</a>.</p>
<p>From 8 to 10 August, other towns and cities in England (including <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton" title="Wolverhampton">Wolverhampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich" title="West Bromwich">West Bromwich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool, England">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">Salford</a>) saw what was described by the media as "<a href="/wiki/Copycat_crime" title="Copycat crime">copycat</a> violence". <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">Social media</a> sites including <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> also featured rumours of further disturbances or details surrounding known disturbances which were later proven to be inaccurate; for instance there were rumours of disturbances in the town of <a href="/wiki/Dudley" title="Dudley">Dudley</a> and at the nearby <a href="/wiki/Merry_Hill_Shopping_Centre" title="Merry Hill Shopping Centre">Merry Hill Shopping Centre</a>, but no incidents in these areas were detected by police. Rumours of a hospital being targeted by rioters in Birmingham were also proven to be wrong, as were rumours of disturbances in the <a href="/wiki/Heath_Town" title="Heath Town">Heath Town</a> district of Wolverhampton, which had witnessed a serious riot more than 20 years earlier.</p>
<p>By 15 August, more than 3,000 arrests had been made across England, with more than 1,000 people issued with criminal charges for various offences related to the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc15Aug_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc15Aug-13">[13]</a></sup> Initially, courts sat for extended hours. There were a total of 3,443 crimes across London that were linked to the disorder.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Along with the five deaths, at least 16 others were injured<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> as a direct result of related violent acts. An estimated £200 million worth of property damage was incurred, and local economic activity was significantly compromised.</p>
<p>The online video website <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> was soon host to much video footage of the riots,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> which had been recorded by witnesses and participants. The riots have generated significant ongoing debate among political, social and academic figures about the causes and context in which they happened. Attributions for the rioters' behaviour include structural factors such as racism, classism, and economic decline, as well as cultural factors like criminality, hooliganism, breakdown of social morality, and gang culture.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_figures_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_figures-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc15Aug_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc15Aug-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-06-duggan_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-06-duggan-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Celebrity_involvement"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Celebrity involvement</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_shooting_of_Mark_Duggan">Police shooting of Mark Duggan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Police shooting of Mark Duggan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark-duggan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cb/Mark-duggan.jpg/220px-Mark-duggan.jpg" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cb/Mark-duggan.jpg/330px-Mark-duggan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/cb/Mark-duggan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="340" data-file-height="386" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark-duggan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mark Duggan</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferry_Lane,_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg/220px-Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg/330px-Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg/440px-Ferry_Lane%2C_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferry_Lane,_Tottenham_Hale_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1767129.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferry Lane, Tottenham Hale, location of the shooting</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Mark_Duggan" title="Death of Mark Duggan">Death of Mark Duggan</a></div>
<p>On Thursday 4 August 2011, a police officer shot and killed 29-year-old Mark Duggan during an intelligence-led, targeted vehicle stop procedure on the Ferry Lane bridge next to <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hale_station" title="Tottenham Hale station">Tottenham Hale station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc2nd_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2nd-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Laville07_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laville07-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Mark-Duggan_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Mark-Duggan-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Independent_Police_Complaints_Commission" title="Independent Police Complaints Commission">Independent Police Complaints Commission</a> (IPCC) said that the planned arrest was part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Trident_(Metropolitan_Police)" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Trident (Metropolitan Police)">Operation Trident</a>, which at that time investigated gun crime within the <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">black community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-06-duggan_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-06-duggan-17">[17]</a></sup> The incident had been referred to the IPCC,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc2nd_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2nd-18">[18]</a></sup> which is standard practice if death or serious injury follows police contact.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the shooting, the media widely reported that a bullet was found embedded in a police radio, implying that Duggan fired on the police.<sup id="cite_ref-Laville07_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laville07-19">[19]</a></sup> Friends and relatives of Duggan said that he was unarmed. The police later revealed that initial <a href="/wiki/Ballistics" title="Ballistics">ballistics</a> tests on the bullet recovered from the police radio indicate that it was a "very distinct" police issue <a href="/wiki/Hollow-point_bullet" title="Hollow-point bullet">hollow-point bullet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Laville07_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laville07-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The IPCC later stated that a loaded Bruni BBM blank-firing pistol, converted to fire live ammunition, was recovered from the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It was wrapped in a sock and there was no evidence that it had been fired.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg/220px-Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg/330px-Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg/440px-Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tottenham_Riot-shops.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A shop in Tottenham Hale Retail park after the looting</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 13 August, the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Police_Complaints_Commission" title="Independent Police Complaints Commission">Independent Police Complaints Commission</a> stated that Duggan did not open fire: "It seems possible that we may have verbally led journalists to [wrongly] believe that shots were exchanged". The bullet that had lodged in an officer's radio is believed to have been an <a href="/wiki/Overpenetration" class="mw-redirect" title="Overpenetration">overpenetration</a>, having passed through Duggan's body.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>At lunchtime on 6 August, seven hours before the march and subsequent riot took place, a meeting was called by police between local community leaders, councillors and members of police advisory groups. In this meeting, police were warned several times that there could possibly be another riot similar to the <a href="/wiki/Broadwater_Farm_riot" title="Broadwater Farm riot">Broadwater Farm riot</a> of 1985 if local concerns regarding the death were not addressed.<sup id="cite_ref-channel4ex_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channel4ex-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcreport_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcreport-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 January 2014, a jury at the Royal Courts of Justice came to the conclusion, by a majority of eight to two, that Duggan was lawfully killed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protest_march">Protest march</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Protest march">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On Saturday 6 August a protest was held, initially peacefully, beginning at <a href="/wiki/Broadwater_Farm" title="Broadwater Farm">Broadwater Farm</a> and finishing at Tottenham police station.<sup id="cite_ref-bolesworth_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bolesworth-32">[32]</a></sup> The protest was organised by friends and relatives of Duggan to demand justice for the family.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-06-duggan_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-06-duggan-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Rioting occurred shortly after about 120 people marched from the Broadwater Farm estate to Tottenham Police Station via the High Road.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The group of some 300 people demanded that a senior local police officer come out to speak to them. When Chief Inspector Ade Adelekan arrived, he was met with boos and cries of "murderer", "<a href="/wiki/Uncle_Tom#Epithet" title="Uncle Tom">Uncle Tom</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_slurs#C" title="List of ethnic slurs">coconut</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The crowd stayed in front of the police station hours longer than they originally planned because they were not satisfied with the seniority of the officers available at the time. Rumours that a 16-year-old girl had sustained injuries after attacking police with a champagne bottle began circulating on social media. To date, the girl remains unidentified and the report unconfirmed, however the rumour alone was sufficient to further fuel tensions in the area<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jackson_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jackson-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Riots">Riots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Riots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2011_England_riots" title="Timeline of the 2011 England riots">Timeline of the 2011 England riots</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg/220px-Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg/330px-Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg/440px-Fireman_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath-crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="875" data-file-height="583" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

A firefighter douses a blaze in Tottenham during the aftermath of the initial riot</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg/220px-Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg/330px-Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg/440px-Tottenham_riots_August_6th.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_London_riots.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/2011_London_riots.jpg/220px-2011_London_riots.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/2011_London_riots.jpg/330px-2011_London_riots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/2011_London_riots.jpg/440px-2011_London_riots.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3577" data-file-height="2376" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg/220px-Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg/330px-Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg/440px-Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2667" data-file-height="1778" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barclays_-_2011_London_Looting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bank workers in Walthamstow observe the destruction which was caused in the early hours of the morning</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg/220px-Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg/330px-Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg/440px-Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_Riots_2011_burnt_cars.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burnt-out cars in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg/220px-Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg/330px-Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg/440px-Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2325" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Croydon_Riots_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stand-off between rioters and police in Croydon</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A peaceful march on Saturday 6 August in Tottenham was followed by rioting and looting, first in Tottenham and later in Tottenham Hale Retail Park.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_timeline_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_timeline-39">[39]</a></sup> The spread of news and rumours about the previous evening's disturbances in Tottenham sparked riots during the night of Sunday 7 August in the London districts of Brixton, Enfield, Islington and <a href="/wiki/Wood_Green" title="Wood Green">Wood Green</a> and in Oxford Circus in the centre of London.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_timeline_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_timeline-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The morning of Monday 8 August was quiet, but by evening, areas across London were affected by widespread looting, arson and violence, with significant outbreaks in parts of Battersea, Brixton, Bromley, Camden, Croydon, Ealing, East Ham, Hackney, Harrow, Lewisham, Peckham, Stratford, Waltham Forest, Woolwich, and Wood Green. A man was found shot in Croydon, and died later in hospital. Another man who had been assaulted in Ealing died in hospital on Thursday 11 August. Similar riots were reported outside London – notably in Birmingham, Bristol, Gloucester, Gillingham and Nottingham.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_timeline_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_timeline-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a greatly increased police presence, London was quiet on Tuesday 9 August, but rioting continued in Nottingham and Birmingham (where, according to the police account, eleven shots were fired at police, including at a police helicopter, and petrol bombs thrown at officers<sup id="cite_ref-WMP_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMP-41">[41]</a></sup>) and spread to Leicester, parts of the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(county)" title="West Midlands (county)">West Midlands</a> and to parts of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a> in the north-west of England.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_timeline_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_timeline-39">[39]</a></sup> On Wednesday 10 August, London remained quiet while hundreds of arrests were being made by the police. Three men were killed in Birmingham in a hit-and-run incident related to the disturbances. Looting and violence continued in two locations around Manchester and Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_timeline_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_timeline-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_media">Social media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Social media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Throughout the rioting, many of the rioters failed to cover their faces. Some posed for pictures with stolen goods, posting them on social-networking sites.<sup id="cite_ref-Tom_de_Castella_.26_Caroline_McClatchey_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tom_de_Castella_.26_Caroline_McClatchey-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although London employs CCTV cameras to monitor crime and large events, reports indicate that citizen footage contributed more to capturing looters in action than the police force.<sup id="cite_ref-London_and_England_riots:_CCTV_Pictures_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_and_England_riots:_CCTV_Pictures-43">[43]</a></sup> Beyond the CCTV, looters were filmed and photographed with their faces visible. Police forces and investigators used websites like <a href="/wiki/Flickr" title="Flickr">Flickr</a> to find galleries of the looters to help solve and prevent cases of vandalism and further damage. <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> pages were also created to identify looters.<sup id="cite_ref-Citizen_Cameras_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citizen_Cameras-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several interactive maps were implemented in the <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a> website that showed satellite views of what was happening in the streets during the rioting. James Cridland, the managing director of the free media resources, created a Google Map that tracked verified locations of rioting. <a href="/wiki/Channel_4_News" title="Channel 4 News">Channel 4 News</a> also had similar maps that progressively tracked the damage in the streets as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Interactive_Maps_reveal_satellite.27s_view_of_UK_Riots_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interactive_Maps_reveal_satellite.27s_view_of_UK_Riots-45">[45]</a></sup> News channels also were able to utilise this public service to capture live footage on the streets and inform citizens of dangerous or crowded areas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BlackBerry_Messenger">BlackBerry Messenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: BlackBerry Messenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were reports that the <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Messenger" title="BlackBerry Messenger">BlackBerry Messenger</a> service was used by looters to organise their activities, and that inflammatory and inaccurate accounts of Mark Duggan's killing on social media sites may have incited disturbances.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-G8AUG2011_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G8AUG2011-48">[48]</a></sup> One of the many messages shared between users was the following:</p>
<dl>
<dd>"Everyone in edmonton enfield wood green everywhere in north link up at enfield town station at 4 o clock sharp!!!!," it began. "Start leaving ur yards n linking up with your niggas. Fuck da feds, bring your ballys and your bags trollys, cars vans, hammers the lot!!"<sup id="cite_ref-guardian4_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian4-49">[49]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>Research in Motion assisted British police in tracking rioters who used BBM, stating, "We comply with the Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act and co-operate fully with the Home Office and UK police forces."<sup id="cite_ref-garside1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garside1-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Increased connectivity among individuals has led to a greater ability to organise and execute massive gatherings.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> This has not occurred only with the riots in England, but with other collective gatherings such as the Arab Spring and the Egyptian revolution of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twitter">Twitter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Twitter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Much like BBM, the mobility of technology shaped the London riots. During the Tottenham riots of 1985, citizens had to head into a public place to voice their message.<sup id="cite_ref-Adams_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adams-53">[53]</a></sup> Yet, with access to Twitter as a communication medium, social media was used to rapidly spread messages of the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-Adams_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adams-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Radio 4 criticised Twitter's contribution to the riots through greed and criminality.<sup id="cite_ref-Williams_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-54">[54]</a></sup> <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> described Twitter as being an outlet for promoting gang violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Williams_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-54">[54]</a></sup> Evidence shows that Twitter is powerful because tweets of individuals were inspired by news content.<sup id="cite_ref-Tonkin_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonkin-55">[55]</a></sup> However, an article in <i>Time</i> magazine suggested BlackBerry Messenger was more to blame.<sup id="cite_ref-Adams_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adams-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the riots, Twitter accounted for four out of every 170 UK Internet visits on Monday 8 August. As shown in the London riots, Twitter users send a message to millions. Data collected from the London riots displayed Twitter as a tool to support one's point and Tweets made popular by newsworthy people.<sup id="cite_ref-Tonkin_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonkin-55">[55]</a></sup> Twitter is an effective communication medium with its simple tools such as re-tweeting and hashtags, making it effortless for users to spread a message.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang-56">[56]</a></sup> The hashtag system allows people to band together under a common cause without having previously met.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang-56">[56]</a></sup> In addition, citizens also used Twitter to band together, after the destruction. The aftermath of the riots resulted in a disrupted city, yet Twitter was further used to maintain peace, with hashtags including "#riotcleanup".<sup id="cite_ref-Tonkin_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonkin-55">[55]</a></sup> Another prominent tool includes retweeting and having one clear message heard. Evidence shows that people were tweeting and re-tweeting news related to the riots, not original content.<sup id="cite_ref-Tonkin_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonkin-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_phones">Mobile phones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobile phones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other than BlackBerry Messenger and social networking sites, mobile phone operators T-Mobile and Orange prioritised police requests for information about the phones that were used to plan the riots that hit British cities. Under the <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_Investigatory_Powers_Act_2000" title="Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act 2000">Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act</a>, phone companies were required to hand over data about the locations calls were made from, the owners of phones, and lists of calls made to and from a particular handset.<sup id="cite_ref-garside1_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garside1-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:640px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Firemen_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath.ogv/639px--Firemen_in_action_at_Tottenham_riots_2011_aftermath.ogv.jpg&quot; A burnt-out building being doused with water. Built for the London Co-operative Society in 1930 as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.apcg29.dsl.pipex.com/new%20goal%20for%20tottenham%20store.htm">Union Point</a>, the building included a <a href="/wiki/Carpetright" title="Carpetright">Carpetright</a> on the ground floor and many flats on the upper storeys.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deaths_and_injuries">Deaths and injuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Deaths and injuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trevor_Ellis">Trevor Ellis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Trevor Ellis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Trevor Ellis, a 26-year-old from <a href="/wiki/Brixton_Hill" title="Brixton Hill">Brixton Hill</a>, died following a shooting in <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_London" title="South London">South London</a> on 8 August.<sup id="cite_ref-death_one_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_one-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> His family denied reports that Ellis, who had come from the Brixton area to Croydon with a group of friends, had been involved in looting.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> By 16 December 2013, 13 people had been arrested in connection with the murder. All have later been bailed and then released without action. On 16 December, the eve of Ellis's birthday, detectives opened up a fresh appeal into the murder, asking for witnesses to come forward. No one has yet<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> been charged.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Haroon_Jahan.2C_Shahzad_Ali_and_Abdul_Musavir">Haroon Jahan, Shahzad Ali and Abdul Musavir</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Haroon Jahan, Shahzad Ali and Abdul Musavir">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 10 August, in <a href="/wiki/Winson_Green" title="Winson Green">Winson Green</a>, Birmingham, three men – Haroon Jahan, 21, and brothers Shahzad Ali, 30, and Abdul Musavir, 31 – were killed in a <a href="/wiki/Hit_and_run_(vehicular)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hit and run (vehicular)">hit-and-run incident</a> while attempting to protect their neighbourhood from rioters and looters.<sup id="cite_ref-death_two_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_two-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-death_three_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_three-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On 19 April 2012, a trial of eight men, each <a href="/wiki/Arraignment" title="Arraignment">arraigned</a> on three counts of murder, was held in the Crown Court at Birmingham before Mr Justice Flaux; the jury acquitted all of the defendants on all charges.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Richard_Mannington_Bowes">Richard Mannington Bowes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Richard Mannington Bowes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg/220px-Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg/330px-Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg/440px-Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2337" data-file-height="3268" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Springbridge_Mews_floral_tributes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Floral tributes at the site of the fatal assault. The flowers at the top spell out the word "why".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A 68-year-old man, Richard Mannington Bowes, died on 11 August after he was attacked while attempting to stamp out a litter-bin fire in <a href="/wiki/Ealing" title="Ealing">Ealing</a> on the evening of 8 August.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bowes was attacked by members of a mob on 8 August 2011, while attempting to extinguish a fire that had been <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">deliberately started</a> in industrial bins on Spring Bridge Road. The attack inflicted severe head injuries which resulted in a coma. The assault was caught on <a href="/wiki/CCTV" class="mw-redirect" title="CCTV">CCTV</a> and reportedly filmed on mobile phones by associates of the alleged assailant.<sup id="cite_ref-sun_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sun-66">[66]</a></sup> The attack on Bowes was witnessed by several police officers, but due to the number of rioters they were unable to come to his aid until riot squad officers pushed back the rioters while being attacked to reach Bowes. A line of officers then held back the rioters as paramedics arrived. Bowes's wallet and phone had been stolen, and police faced difficulty in identifying him. He died of his injuries in <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Hospital,_London" title="St Mary's Hospital, London">St Mary's Hospital</a> on 11 August 2011 after being removed from life support.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many tributes were paid to Bowes, including Ealing Council who flew the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> at half-mast over its town hall and announced the launch of a relief fund in his name,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-69">[69]</a></sup> and London Mayor <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>, who described him as a hero.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 16-year-old male, later named as Darrell Desuze,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> who lives in <a href="/wiki/Hounslow" title="Hounslow">Hounslow</a> was charged with murdering Bowes, violent disorder and four burglaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_charged_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_charged-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> He appeared at <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a> <a href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_Court_(England_and_Wales)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magistrates' Court (England and Wales)">Magistrates' Court</a> on 16 August 2011, where he was remanded in custody until his appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">Central Criminal Court</a> on 18 August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_charged_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_charged-72">[72]</a></sup> His 31-year-old mother Lavinia Desuze<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> was charged with perverting the course of justice.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_charged_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_charged-72">[72]</a></sup> On 12 March 2012 at the Crown Court at Inner London, Darrel Desuze pleaded guilty to manslaughter, after previously pleading guilty to burglary and violent disorder.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The following day the Crown withdrew the murder charge against him.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> After a trial at the Crown Court at Inner London before <a href="/wiki/John_Saunders_(English_judge)" title="John Saunders (English judge)">Mr Justice Saunders</a> and a jury, Lavinia Desuze was convicted of perverting the course of justice after she destroyed the clothing her son wore on the day of the death.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On 17 April 2012, Mr Justice Saunders sentenced Darrell Desuze to detention for a term of eight years, and Lavinia Desuze to imprisonment for eighteen months.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Injuries">Injuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Injuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Hackney,_2011_riots.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg/220px-Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg/330px-Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg/440px-Welcome_to_Hackney%2C_2011_riots.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Hackney,_2011_riots.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A burnt-out and vandalised car in Hackney with misspelt graffiti. Arsonists set fire to 12 cars during the riots.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg/220px-Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg/330px-Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg/440px-Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg 2x" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="698" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Double-deck_burning_in_2011_england_riots.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Double-decker bus burning in Tottenham during the 2011 England riots, in which arsonists set fire to 4 buses.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In London, between Monday afternoon and the early hours of Tuesday, 14 people were injured by rioters. These included a 75-year-old woman who suffered a broken hip in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hackney" title="London Borough of Hackney">Hackney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-independent_injuries_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_injuries-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Barking" title="Barking">Barking</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_(London_sub_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="East (London sub region)">East London</a>, 20-year-old <a href="/wiki/Malaysians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Malaysians in the United Kingdom">Malaysian</a> student Ashraf Rossli was beaten and then robbed twice by looters emptying his rucksack. Footage of the second mugging, which appears to show the second set of muggers pretend to help him then proceed to ransack his rucksack, was uploaded onto YouTube. He suffered a broken jaw, requiring surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_mugging_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_mugging-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-79">[79]</a></sup> On 2 March 2012, two men, John Kafunda of <a href="/wiki/Ilford" title="Ilford">Ilford</a> and Reece Donovan of <a href="/wiki/Romford" title="Romford">Romford</a>, were found guilty of the robbery of Rossli and also violent disorder by a jury at Wood Green Crown Court.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The sentences were quashed by the Court of Appeal on 29 November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chingford" title="Chingford">Chingford</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_(London_sub_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="East (London sub region)">East London</a>, three police officers were hit by a car used as a getaway vehicle by a group who looted the Aristocrat store on Chingford Mount Road. Two of the officers were seriously injured and taken to hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In total, 186 police officers were injured<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_figures_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_figures-9">[9]</a></sup> as well as 3 <a href="/wiki/Police_Community_Support_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Police Community Support Officer">Police Community Support Officers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pcs.org.uk_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcs.org.uk-8">[8]</a></sup> Five police dogs were also reported injured.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ten firefighters were injured as the <a href="/wiki/London_Fire_Brigade" title="London Fire Brigade">London Fire Brigade</a> dealt with over 100 serious fires caused by the disturbances. The LFB also reported that eight of its <a href="/wiki/London_Fire_Brigade_appliances" title="London Fire Brigade appliances">fire engines</a> had their windscreens smashed and that two <a href="/wiki/Fire_chief%27s_vehicle" title="Fire chief's vehicle">fire cars</a> were attacked.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Property_and_business_damage">Property and business damage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Property and business damage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vehicles, homes and shops were attacked and set alight. At least 100 homes were destroyed in the arson and looting.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Shopkeepers estimated the damages in their Tottenham Hale and Tottenham branches at several million pounds.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The riots caused the irretrievable loss of heritage architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> It was estimated that retailers lost at least 30,000 trading hours.<sup id="cite_ref-Tele_24_August_2011_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tele_24_August_2011-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg/220px-Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg" width="220" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg/330px-Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg/440px-Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="963" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cash_Converters_on_Salford_Precinct_riot_damage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cash Converters shop in Salford</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Association of British Insurers said they expect the industry to pay out in excess of £200&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Estimated losses in London were indicated to be in the region of £100m.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg/220px-Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg/330px-Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg/440px-Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reeves_furniture_store_burnt_out.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The remains of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Reeves" title="House of Reeves">House of Reeves</a> shop in <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 8 August 2011, a <a href="/wiki/Sony_Digital_Audio_Disc_Corporation" title="Sony Digital Audio Disc Corporation">Sony DADC</a> warehouse in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Enfield" title="London Borough of Enfield">Enfield</a> at <a href="/wiki/Enfield_Lock" title="Enfield Lock">Enfield Lock</a>, which also acted as the primary distribution centre for <a href="/wiki/Independent_music" title="Independent music">independent music</a> distributor <a href="/wiki/PIAS_Entertainment_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="PIAS Entertainment Group">PIAS Entertainment Group</a>, was destroyed by fire.<sup id="cite_ref-piasfire_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piasfire-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-92">[92]</a></sup> Initially, because millions of items of stock were lost, including most of PIAS's inventory, it was thought that long-term damage to the British independent music industry might result.<sup id="cite_ref-piasfire_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piasfire-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-piasbbc_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piasbbc-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-piasloss_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piasloss-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-piasfund_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piasfund-95">[95]</a></sup> On 18 August 2011, PIAS confirmed that their operations were back to normal.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> On 11 August 2011, London police reported that they had arrested three teenagers in connection with the warehouse fire.<sup id="cite_ref-psarr_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psarr-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Financial Times</i> reported that an analysis showed that 48,000 local businesses – shops, restaurants, pubs and clubs – had suffered financial losses as a result of the looting and rioting in English streets.<sup id="cite_ref-FT12AUG2011_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT12AUG2011-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_attacks_and_thefts">Personal attacks and thefts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personal attacks and thefts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 15-year-old was accused in August 2011 of raping a 13-year-old girl while the riots were taking place. The prosecution described the incident as being geographically "close" to the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_courts_struggle_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_courts_struggle-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Twenty-year-old student Ashraf Haziq was attacked while cycling along Queen's Road in <a href="/wiki/Barking" title="Barking">Barking</a>. The prosecution said that the victim was punched in the face by one of a group of 100 youths. His bike, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> and mobile phone were stolen.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_courts_struggle_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_courts_struggle-99">[99]</a></sup> In September 2011, an accusation of robbery was made against 24-year-old Reece Donovan. The same month, a 17-year-old was accused in court of breaking the victim's jaw with an unprovoked punch.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_accused_punching_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_accused_punching-100">[100]</a></sup> In February 2012 John Kafunda and Reece Donovan were convicted of stealing from Rossli, after being identified on camera pretending to help him.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_guilty_stealing_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_guilty_stealing-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Four London buses were set on fire during the riots.</p>
<ul>
<li>Evening of 6 August: Arriva London North DAF DB250L/Alexander ALX400 double decker DLA284 (Y484 UGC) was destroyed on Tottenham High Road.</li>
<li>Evening of 8 August: Abellio London Dennis Trident/Alexander ALX400 double decker 9755 (YN51 KVM) was destroyed at Reeves Corner, Croydon.</li>
<li>Late afternoon of 8 August: Go Ahead London Central Volvo B9TL/Wright Gemini 2 double decker WVL302 (LX59 CZV) was set alight in Peckham, but not destroyed. This bus has been rebuilt and re-entered service at New Cross bus garage on 31 May 2012.</li>
<li>Late afternoon of 8 August: First Capital Dennis Dart SLF/Caetano Nimbus single decker DMC41496 (LK03 NMF) was set alight at Dalston, but not destroyed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Many other London buses were damaged with broken windows etc.</p>
<p>On 9 August, Croydon's <a href="/wiki/Tramlink" title="Tramlink">Tramlink</a> was partly shut down due to damage inflicted along its route.<sup id="cite_ref-thisislondon1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisislondon1-102">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Overground" title="London Overground">London Overground</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> shut Barking, Peckham Rye and Harrow-on-the-Hill and Hackney Central stations. The train operating company <a href="/wiki/Southern_(train_operating_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern (train operating company)">Southern</a> later announced that trains were not stopping at many stations in south London.<sup id="cite_ref-thisislondon1_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisislondon1-102">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express Coaches</a> stopped serving Wolverhampton and suburban stops in the Birmingham area (but not <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Coach_Station" title="Birmingham Coach Station">Birmingham Coach Station</a> itself) and Manchester (but not Manchester Airport).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_fixtures">Sporting fixtures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sporting fixtures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Five <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> games due to be played on 9 and 10 August were postponed after requests from police due to the riots. The games at <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> were all postponed, as they were all situated within a short distance of areas which had seen some of the worst disturbances.<sup id="cite_ref-West_Ham-Aldershot_Carling_Cup_tie_postponed_on_police_advice_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_Ham-Aldershot_Carling_Cup_tie_postponed_on_police_advice-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-London_riots_hit_sports_fixtures_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_riots_hit_sports_fixtures-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charlton-Reading_Carling_Cup_match_called_off_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charlton-Reading_Carling_Cup_match_called_off-106">[106]</a></sup> There was also uncertainty as to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_cricket_team_in_England_in_2011" title="Indian cricket team in England in 2011">Third Test cricket match</a> between <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Edgbaston_Cricket_Ground" title="Edgbaston Cricket Ground">Edgbaston</a> in Birmingham, but the match was played.<sup id="cite_ref-London_riots_continue.2C_Birmingham_test_in_jeopardy_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_riots_continue.2C_Birmingham_test_in_jeopardy-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Test_set_to_begin_despite_riots_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Test_set_to_begin_despite_riots-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly match</a> between <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> due to take place on 10 August was cancelled,<sup id="cite_ref-London_riots_hit_sports_fixtures_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_riots_hit_sports_fixtures-105">[105]</a></sup> as well as the international friendly between <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> scheduled for 9 August at <a href="/wiki/Vicarage_Road" title="Vicarage Road">Vicarage Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghana_versus_Nigeria_friendly_in_Watford_called_off_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana_versus_Nigeria_friendly_in_Watford_called_off-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Four_Carling_Cup_ties_postponed_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Four_Carling_Cup_ties_postponed-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>'s opening game of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">2011–12 Premier League</a> season against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on 13 August was postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-Tottenham_v_Everton_match_postponed_after_London_riots_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tottenham_v_Everton_match_postponed_after_London_riots-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The League Two game between <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Town_F.C." title="Cheltenham Town F.C.">Cheltenham Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swindon_Town_F.C." title="Swindon Town F.C.">Swindon Town</a>, due to be played the same day, was also initially postponed until further consultation allowed Gloucestershire Police to provide the required resources.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political">Political</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Political">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the initial disorder in Tottenham, the <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Tottenham (UK Parliament constituency)">constituency</a> <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> MP <a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a> appealed for calm, saying that "true justice can only follow a thorough investigation of the facts"<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and that Tottenham had had its "heart ripped out" by the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph1_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-115">[115]</a></sup> He said that rioters were not representative of the local community as a whole<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-116">[116]</a></sup> and insisted that the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Police_Complaints_Commission" title="Independent Police Complaints Commission">Independent Police Complaints Commission</a> must fully establish the circumstances of Mark Duggan's death.<sup id="cite_ref-lammy_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lammy-117">[117]</a></sup> Lammy voiced concerns that the <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">EDL</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_National_Party" title="British National Party">BNP</a> were playing on the London riots and people's fears to advance their political motives.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Streatham_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Streatham (UK Parliament constituency)">Streatham</a>'s Labour MP <a href="/wiki/Chuka_Umunna" title="Chuka Umunna">Chuka Umunna</a> condemned the violence in Brixton and Tottenham.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian3_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian3-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yourlocalguardian1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yourlocalguardian1-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-streathamguardian1_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-streathamguardian1-121">[121]</a></sup> Umunna called for the <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Messenger" title="BlackBerry Messenger">BlackBerry Messenger</a> service, used by some of the rioters to co-ordinate their activities, to be "temporarily disabled" between 6&#160;pm and 6&#160;am <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>The use of BlackBerry Messenger has led to arrests – a <a href="/wiki/Colchester" title="Colchester">Colchester</a> man was detained under the Serious Crimes Act for organising a water-fight through the service.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Randall_(British_politician)" title="John Randall (British politician)">John Randall</a>, the Conservative MP for Uxbridge and South Ruislip said: "It’s a small minority of people causing the trouble. The events in Ealing brought it home, it’s just down the Uxbridge Road."<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hackney_North_and_Stoke_Newington_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hackney North and Stoke Newington (UK Parliament constituency)">Hackney North and Stoke Newington</a> MP <a href="/wiki/Diane_Abbott" title="Diane Abbott">Diane Abbott</a> called for the introduction of a <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Newark_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Newark (UK Parliament constituency)">Newark</a> MP <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Colonel (United Kingdom)">Colonel</a> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Mercer" title="Patrick Mercer">Patrick Mercer</a> called for the deployment of <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In December 2010 <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, the Home Secretary, had said that the deployment of water cannon by police forces on the British mainland was an operational decision which had been "resisted until now by senior police officers."<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> On 9 August 2011, May rejected their use and said: "The way we police in Britain is not through use of water cannon. The way we police in Britain is through consent of communities." <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a>, the former London mayor, said "The issue of water cannon would be very useful given the level of arson we are seeing here." Scotland Yard said officers did not have any water cannon and if their use was approved they would have to be brought over from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>May said: "I condemn utterly the violence in Tottenham... Such disregard for public safety and property will not be tolerated, and the Metropolitan Police have my full support in restoring order."<sup id="cite_ref-patrol-streets_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patrol-streets-128">[128]</a></sup> She returned to the UK from holiday early to meet senior police officials on 8 August.</p>
<p>A spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/10_Downing_Street#Prime_Minister.27s_Office" title="10 Downing Street">Prime Minister's office</a> added: "The rioting in Tottenham last night was utterly unacceptable. There is no justification for the aggression the police and the public faced, or for the damage to property."<sup id="cite_ref-patrol-streets_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patrol-streets-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">deputy prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a> said that the riots were "completely unacceptable" and described the rioters as "needless and opportunistic".<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>London's mayor, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>, who cut short a holiday in Canada to return to the UK on 9 August, said: "I'm appalled at the scenes of violence and destruction in Tottenham"<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-116">[116]</a></sup> whilst his deputy <a href="/wiki/Kit_Malthouse" title="Kit Malthouse">Kit Malthouse</a> told a <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a> reporter that "criminal elements were to blame for the trouble."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> condemned the "terrible scenes of people looting, vandalizing, thieving, robbing" and told rioters "You will feel the full force of the law. And if you are old enough to commit these crimes, you are old enough to face the punishment."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_news_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_news-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Croydon_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Croydon Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Croydon Central</a> MP <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Barwell" title="Gavin Barwell">Gavin Barwell</a> called the damage caused in the London Borough of Croydon "sickening".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a strongly worded criticism of what he deems to be a misplaced "hyper-sensitivity about race", dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Macpherson_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Macpherson Report">Macpherson Report</a> of 1999, <a href="/wiki/Civitas_(think_tank)" title="Civitas (think tank)">Civitas</a> director David Green attributed the reluctance by police to use force to a fear of disciplinary action. He said that "officers in charge of a riot think it safer to wait for orders from the top".<sup id="cite_ref-DavidGreen_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DavidGreen-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a public speech on 15 August, David Cameron blamed a "broken society" in "moral collapse"<sup id="cite_ref-Broken_Society_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broken_Society-134">[134]</a></sup> – broad societal change themes common to his party's election campaign theme <a href="/wiki/Broken_Britain" title="Broken Britain">Broken Britain</a>.</p>
<p>The city councils of Manchester and Salford are reported to be investigating their powers for ways of evicting tenants if they, or their children, have been involved in violence or looting in their cities.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_eviction_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_eviction-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Borough_of_Greenwich" title="Royal Borough of Greenwich">London Borough of Greenwich</a> also stated on its website: "We shall seek the eviction of anyone living in council property if they are found to have been engaged in criminal acts."<sup id="cite_ref-Greenwich_Council_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenwich_Council-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several countries issued warnings advising caution to travellers visiting the United Kingdom during the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>German <a href="/wiki/Far-left_politics" title="Far-left politics">far-left</a> activists suggested using the riots as a <a href="/wiki/Role_model" title="Role model">role model</a> to be applied to their political activities in Germany as well.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press">Press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The riots were described by one journalist as "the worst disturbances of their kind since the <a href="/wiki/1995_Brixton_riot" title="1995 Brixton riot">1995 Brixton riots</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jackson_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jackson-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
