<p>Commentators likened the riots to the <a href="/wiki/Broadwater_Farm_riot" title="Broadwater Farm riot">Broadwater Farm riot</a> of 1985, during which a police officer, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Keith_Blakelock" title="Death of Keith Blakelock">Keith Blakelock</a>, was murdered.<sup id="cite_ref-lammy_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lammy-117">[117]</a></sup> The disturbances were preceded by calls for better oversight of the Metropolitan Police, repeating observations which go back to the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Stephen_Lawrence" class="mw-redirect" title="Death of Stephen Lawrence">death of Stephen Lawrence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_Cross_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="New Cross Fire">New Cross Fire</a>. In April 2011<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> there was a large nonviolent march to <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Yard" title="Scotland Yard">Scotland Yard</a> as a result of the death of <a href="/wiki/Smiley_Culture" title="Smiley Culture">Smiley Culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The very widespread scale of the violence prompted comparisons with the <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Riots" title="Gordon Riots">Gordon Riots</a> of 1780.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> called the scenes "shameful" and lamented that "[w]ith the London Olympics less than a year away, our reputation is being damaged at the worst moment". It added: "This is anarchy, pure and simple. And it presents a serious threat to life and property."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s editorial said: "What we have experienced in London and elsewhere since Saturday night is a wholly new phenomenon: violent disorder whose sole intent is criminal... In such circumstances, there can be only one response if the law-abiding majority is to be protected: the thugs must be taught to respect the law of the land the hard way."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Telegraph</i> also reported: "Tottenham riots: police let gangs run riot and loot: Britain’s biggest police force is facing criticism after it let looters run riot in north London for almost 12 hours..."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> called on the public to back the police: "... Britain's 2011 riots have become a defining contest between disorder and order. In that contest, important caveats notwithstanding, there is only one right side to be on. The attacks, the destruction, the criminality and the reign of fear must be stopped. The rule of law in the cities of Britain must not only be defended against delinquent destruction. It must also be enforced."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the height of the riots, <i>The Guardian</i> was accused of anti-Semitic incitement by the media monitoring organisation, Comment Is Free Watch (CiFW), after Guardian journalist Paul Lewis singled out <a href="/wiki/Hasidic_Judaism" title="Hasidic Judaism">Hasidic Jewish</a> residents who were not involved in the rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The content of his report stated, "The make-up of the rioters was racially mixed. Most were men or boys, some apparently as young as 10….But families and other local residents, including some from Tottenham's Hasidic Jewish community, also gathered to watch and jeer at police." CIFW responded by condemning the newspaper saying, "A 1,800 Guardian report doesn't mention the race, ethnicity, or religion of the rioters, somehow found it pertinent to note that some of those who gathered to jeer police were, allegedly, Hasidic Jews." As a result of the negative publicity, <i>The Guardian</i> revised the story.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its 9 August leading article, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> said the police's handling of <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Mark_Duggan" title="Death of Mark Duggan">Mark Duggan's death</a> "looks to have been poor", and that there is "context of mistrust of the police here." The paper added that "it is spurious to draw a connection between that disaffection [by the inner-city youth] and specific outbreaks of violence of the sort we have seen in recent days."<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Hitchens" title="Peter Hitchens">Peter Hitchens</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> disputed the idea that the events were riots on the basis that they were fundamentally apolitical. He further stated: "This is an equal-opportunity crime wave. The lawbreakers are not from any distinct ethnic group, and attempts to explain this behaviour on these ground are baseless and poisonous."<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Dalrymple" title="Theodore Dalrymple">Theodore Dalrymple</a> wrote an opinion piece for the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i>, in which he blamed the "sense of entitlement" that he sees as being common among Britain's youth as a cause for the riots, and said that British youth are today among "the most unpleasant and violent in the world" as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-ny_daniels_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ny_daniels-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some journalists made comparisons between these riots and the <a href="/wiki/2005_civil_unrest_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 civil unrest in France">2005 riots in France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In both cases, the unrest started with the death of a young person during a confrontation with the police.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-152">[152]</a></sup> In fact, a television report by <a href="/wiki/France_2" title="France 2">France 2</a>, broadcast in November 2005, showed a visit by a delegation from <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vry,_Essonne" title="Évry, Essonne">Évry</a> (just outside Paris) to <a href="/wiki/Tottenham" title="Tottenham">Tottenham</a>, with the report calling "Tottenham part of London 'regularly shaken by riots' in earlier decades, where 'a lot of money was invested' and 'the promotion of ethnic minorities', had been made a priority."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writing in Pakistan's <i><a href="/wiki/Newsline_(magazine)" title="Newsline (magazine)">Newsline</a></i>, Mahir Ali likened the government's response to that of <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1981_England_riots" title="1981 England riots">1981 England riots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newslinemagazine_trying_to_make_sense_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newslinemagazine_trying_to_make_sense-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public">Public</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre,_2011_riots.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg/220px-Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg/330px-Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg/440px-Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre%2C_2011_riots.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peace_wall_at_Manchester_Arndale_Centre,_2011_riots.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'Peace wall' in the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Arndale_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Arndale Centre">Manchester Arndale Centre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg/170px-The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg/255px-The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg/340px-The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2124" data-file-height="3300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Co-operative_loves_MCR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A number of campaigns were launched, aiming to foster greater civic pride in their cities. Pictured is the <a href="/wiki/CIS_Tower" title="CIS Tower">CIS Tower</a>, Manchester.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many people called for the government to urge the police to deploy anti-riot methods often used outside Great Britain, such as <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bullet" title="Plastic bullet">baton rounds</a> (which have been used in Northern Ireland), the use of which has long been resisted by senior police commanders and politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CapitalFM_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CapitalFM-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pauline Pearce, a 45-year-old woman from Hackney, was filmed close to the rioting, furiously chastising looters over their criminal behaviour.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_jazz_singer_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_jazz_singer-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fearless_hackney_woman_evening_standard_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fearless_hackney_woman_evening_standard-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fearless_hackney_woman_telegraph_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fearless_hackney_woman_telegraph-160">[160]</a></sup> She is seen holding a walking-stick and gesturing.<sup id="cite_ref-fearless_hackney_woman_telegraph_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fearless_hackney_woman_telegraph-160">[160]</a></sup> The resulting <i>Heroine of Hackney</i> video subsequently went <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral</a>. Its rapid spread was helped by <a href="/wiki/Tweeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Tweeting">tweeting</a> from famous people such as newspaper editor <a href="/wiki/Piers_Morgan" title="Piers Morgan">Piers Morgan</a><sup id="cite_ref-fearless_hackney_woman_evening_standard_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fearless_hackney_woman_evening_standard-159">[159]</a></sup> and former Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Prescott" title="John Prescott">John Prescott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-the_sun_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_sun-161">[161]</a></sup> Pearce was hailed as a heroine for helping to ease tensions in Hackney; her influence was acknowledged by politicians<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_history_in_tottenham_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_history_in_tottenham-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-huffington_post_reactionary_ideas_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffington_post_reactionary_ideas-163">[163]</a></sup> and the national press.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_raised_to_rampage_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_raised_to_rampage-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_not_bowed_by_the_mob_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_not_bowed_by_the_mob-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_people_who_defined_week_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_people_who_defined_week-166">[166]</a></sup> MP for <a href="/wiki/Hackney_South_and_Shoreditch_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hackney South and Shoreditch (UK Parliament constituency)">Hackney South and Shoreditch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meg_Hillier" title="Meg Hillier">Meg Hillier</a>, has invited Pearce to the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Houses of Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sundaymirror_why_she_took_a_stand_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaymirror_why_she_took_a_stand-167">[167]</a></sup> Speaking to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i> newspaper, Pearce described the looting and vandalism as being "heart-breaking" and also contrasted people's <a href="/wiki/Relative_poverty" class="mw-redirect" title="Relative poverty">relative poverty</a> with expenditure for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">Olympic Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-the_australian_voice_of_reason_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_australian_voice_of_reason-168">[168]</a></sup> Pearce has since been featured in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectator" title="The Spectator">The Spectator</a></i>, dismissing <a href="/wiki/David_Starkey" title="David Starkey">David Starkey</a>'s view that <a href="/wiki/Hip-hop_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip-hop culture">hip-hop culture</a> was partly to blame for the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-spectator_fifteen_minutes_later_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spectator_fifteen_minutes_later-169">[169]</a></sup> In September 2011, she was awarded the Team London Award at the annual Peace Awards by <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hackneygazette_boris_johnson_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hackneygazette_boris_johnson-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Still_image_from_Hackney_woman_2011_speech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bc/Still_image_from_Hackney_woman_2011_speech.jpg/170px-Still_image_from_Hackney_woman_2011_speech.jpg" width="170" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bc/Still_image_from_Hackney_woman_2011_speech.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="223" data-file-height="341" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Still_image_from_Hackney_woman_2011_speech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Still image from <i>Heroine of Hackney</i> speech</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a>, sales of <a href="/wiki/Baseball_bat" title="Baseball bat">baseball bats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baton_(law_enforcement)" title="Baton (law enforcement)">truncheons</a> increased significantly overnight.<sup id="cite_ref-independent_vigilantes_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_vigilantes-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_neighbourhoods_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_neighbourhoods-172">[172]</a></sup> Deputy Assistant Commissioner Stephen Kavanagh stated: "We are already seeing a community kickback. People are angry. This is their neighbourhoods that are at stake."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_neighbourhoods_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_neighbourhoods-172">[172]</a></sup> Political commentator and foreign affairs analyst <a href="/wiki/Nile_Gardiner" title="Nile Gardiner">Nile Gardiner</a> suggested that the British Government should prompt a debate which will allow British business owners the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_keep_and_bear_arms" title="Right to keep and bear arms">right to keep and bear arms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three men killed in a hit-and-run incident in Birmingham, Haroon Jahan, Shazad Ali, and Abdul Musavir Tariq, were described as heroes for dying while attempting to defend their neighbourhood.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Tariq Jahan, the father of 21-year-old victim Haroon Jahan, gave a speech appealing for calm, social unity and an end to the violence, hours after his son's death. Jahan was hailed as a hero and a patriot for helping to ease tensions in Birmingham; his influence was acknowledged by politicians and the national press, receiving an award at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Pride_of_Britain_Awards" title="Pride of Britain Awards">Pride of Britain Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jahang_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jahang-177">[177]</a></sup> Conservative MEP <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Hannan" title="Daniel Hannan">Daniel Hannan</a> said of him: "Uncomplaining, in control of his emotions, Tariq Jahan reminds us of what it means to be British."<sup id="cite_ref-hannan_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hannan-178">[178]</a></sup> The <i>Financial Times</i> described Jahan as eloquent and inspiring, and said "His selfless intervention contrasted with the rapacious self-interest of the looters, and was a timely reminder of the obligations of community."<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tens of thousands of users of social networking sites coordinated clean-up operations of their local shopping areas and streets. <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">Social media</a> sites Twitter and Facebook were also used for reporting information on the riots and to co-ordinate a voluntary citizens' operation to clear up riot-hit areas.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Clapham_Junction" class="mw-redirect" title="Clapham Junction">Clapham Junction</a>, dozens of volunteers carrying brooms turned out to assist with clean-up efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> On Facebook, over 900,000 people joined a group entitled 'Supporting the Met Police against the London rioters'.<sup id="cite_ref-Tom_de_Castella_.26_Caroline_McClatchey_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tom_de_Castella_.26_Caroline_McClatchey-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manchester City Councillor Pat Karney, the city centre spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_Council" title="Manchester City Council">Manchester City Council</a>, said: "The true Mancunian civic spirit has been shown in Manchester today." Staff from city centre businesses and Manchester Metropolitan University joined the volunteers, as food outlets gave out free drinks and snacks.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> There were several fundraising initiatives to help independent business owners re-build their businesses and livelihoods.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>A petition was submitted to the UK government proposing that any convicted rioters have their benefit payments cut. This petition has been signed by over 200,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>A petition on the UK government website demanding convicted rioters to be banished to the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a> of Scotland was set up in the summer of 2011. The reaction caused a public outcry in Scotland and eventually Westminster offered an apology to <a href="/wiki/Western_Isles" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Isles">Western Isles</a> MP <a href="/wiki/Angus_Brendan_MacNeil" class="mw-redirect" title="Angus Brendan MacNeil">Angus Brendan MacNeil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vigilantism">Vigilantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Vigilantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>By 20:00 on 7 August, the major rioting had spread to <a href="/wiki/Wood_Green" title="Wood Green">Wood Green</a>, but some riot police were on hand.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup> Again, the police did not intervene to stop the looting.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-07-peaceful_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-07-peaceful-16">[16]</a></sup> The mostly <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks in the United Kingdom">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> shop owners along Wood Green, <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_Lane_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Turnpike Lane (London)">Turnpike Lane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_Lanes_(London)" title="Green Lanes (London)">Green Lanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harringay" title="Harringay">Harringay</a>, were said to have formed local 'protection units' around their shops.<sup id="cite_ref-londondailynews_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-londondailynews-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 and 9 August, people from <a href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistani" class="mw-redirect" title="British Pakistani">Pakistani</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Kurds" class="mw-redirect" title="British Kurds">Kurdish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks in the United Kingdom">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> communities chased down masked Black youths in several areas of <a href="/wiki/North_London" title="North London">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_End_of_London" title="East End of London">East London</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Green_Street,_London" title="Green Street, London">Green Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hackney" title="London Borough of Hackney">Hackney</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Haringey" title="London Borough of Haringey">Haringey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">Tower Hamlets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-independent_vigilantes_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_vigilantes-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_neighbourhoods_172-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_neighbourhoods-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Conservative MEP Daniel Hannan praised the community for their brave and responsible reactions to the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-hannan_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hannan-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 August, vigilantes included English locals in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Enfield" title="London Borough of Enfield">Enfield</a> which included several members of the <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">English Defence League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-independent_vigilantes_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_vigilantes-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> locals and supporters of <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall F.C.</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eltham" title="Eltham">Eltham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_neighbourhoods_172-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_neighbourhoods-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_riots_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_riots-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-huff_riots_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huff_riots-196">[196]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Sikhism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Sikhism in the United Kingdom">Sikh communities</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southall" title="Southall">Southall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-independent_vigilantes_171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent_vigilantes-171">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_Ham" title="East Ham">East Ham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilford" title="Ilford">Ilford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romford" title="Romford">Romford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sangat_TV" title="Sangat TV">Sangat TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikh_Channel" title="Sikh Channel">Sikh Channel</a> urged their viewers to protect <a href="/wiki/Gurudwara" class="mw-redirect" title="Gurudwara">Sikh temples</a> after a report that one was attacked in Birmingham.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> On the night of 9–10 August 2011, following violence, arson and rioting in London, members of the Sikh community in Southall volunteered to stand guard at various city <a href="/wiki/Gurdwara" title="Gurdwara">Gurdwaras</a>, with as many as 200 to 300 Sikhs from different age groups gathered in various Gurudwaras across Southall to safeguard their places of worship from rioters.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The Sikhs drew praise from Prime Minister David Cameron for this action.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 August in <a href="/wiki/Eltham" title="Eltham">Eltham</a>, police clashed with a bottle-throwing crowd of about 200 vigilantes, including many <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">English Defence League</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph3_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph3-202">[202]</a></sup> It was reported that 50 EDL members joined forces with locals to patrol the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> That same day, a senior police officer said that some vigilante groups were hampering police operations in London.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianCopycat_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianCopycat-204">[204]</a></sup> 90 EDL members also joined vigilantes in Enfield.<sup id="cite_ref-gwine_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gwine-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_relations">Race relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Race relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The ethnic makeup of the rioters varied in different cities: 76% of those arrested in Manchester were white, while 29% were white and 39% black in London, and the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(county)" title="West Midlands (county)">West Midlands</a> was the only area where more than 6% were Asian.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research conducted by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nottingham" title="University of Nottingham">University of Nottingham</a> suggested that race relations in Britain deteriorated in the period following the riots and that prejudice towards ethnic minorities increased.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> After the hit-and-run incident in Birmingham, in which three Asian men were killed by a black driver, racial tensions between blacks and Asians in Birmingham increased; hostilities were diffused by the public appeals for an end to violence by Tariq Jahan, father of one of the victims.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>The effects of <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black culture</a> were discussed by historian <a href="/wiki/David_Starkey" title="David Starkey">David Starkey</a> in the edition of the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">Newsnight</a></i> TV programme of 12 August. Starkey singled out the influence of black <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangster and rap culture</a> on youths of all races, contrasting contemporary <a href="/wiki/Multicultural_London_English" title="Multicultural London English">youth patois</a> with the speech patterns of black Tottenham MP <a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a>, who, Starkey asserted, "sounded white". The author <a href="/wiki/Dreda_Say_Mitchell" title="Dreda Say Mitchell">Dreda Say Mitchell</a> countered his argument by saying that there is no one single "black culture".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some commentators remarked on the apparently high proportion of black people involved in the riots and took the view that there was a disproportionately high number of rioters who were black, compared to the overall demographics of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-economist-black_community_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-black_community-211">[211]</a></sup> As the Ministry of Justice has admitted "the group of people brought before the courts is only a subset of all people who took part in the public disorder". In February 2012 a report was published by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Justice (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Justice</a> providing demographic statistics of the people charged over participation the riots up to 1 February 2012 which revealed that 41% of those brought before the courts identified themselves as being from the White group, 39% from the Black ethnic group, 12% from the Mixed ethnic group, 6% the Asian ethnic group, and 2% the Other ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> These figures were disproportionate to the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Ethnic groups in the United Kingdom">average UK population</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity-moj_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-moj-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity-sky_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-sky-214">[214]</a></sup> however the figures revealed varying demographics in different areas when compared to local populations. For example, in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Haringey" title="London Borough of Haringey">Haringey</a>, the figures revealed that 55% of defendants in court over riot-related charges were black, compared to a 17% black population; in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a>, 94% of rioters in court were white, compared to an 88% white population, and 6% of rioters were black, compared to a 2% black population.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity-bbc_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-bbc-215">[215]</a></sup> Additionally, looters from 44 foreign countries were jailed, with Jamaicans representing the largest group.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity-star_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-star-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ministry of Justice report also noted that rioters brought before the courts were disproportionately male (89%) and young (53% were aged 20 or under, with the number of "<a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">juveniles</a>" ranging from 26% in London to 39% in <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>, and very few listed as over 40).<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Metropolitan Police Service launched Operation Withern, an investigation into the events leading up to and during the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian2_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2-219">[219]</a></sup> The operation was initially led by <a href="/wiki/Detective_Superintendent" class="mw-redirect" title="Detective Superintendent">Detective Superintendent</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Sweeney_(police_officer)" title="John Sweeney (police officer)">John Sweeney</a> of the Metropolitan Police Service, with detectives from the <a href="/wiki/Homicide_and_Serious_Crime_Command" title="Homicide and Serious Crime Command">Homicide and Serious Crime Command</a>, specialist investigators from the <a href="/wiki/Public_Order_Branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Order Branch">Public Order Branch</a>, and police support staff. Detective Superintendent Robin Bhairam, took over the post event investigation, where officers were drawn from all over the MPS, from different business groups, and placed into 10 Investigation Hubs across London.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> The Deputy Assistant Commissioner of the Metropolitan Police, Steve Kavanagh, stated that the number of officers deployed tripled between 6 and 7 August.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>The BBC reported that West Midlands riot police officers were issued with <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bullets" class="mw-redirect" title="Plastic bullets">plastic bullets</a> to use against looters, but that none were fired.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC6SEP2011_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC6SEP2011-223">[223]</a></sup> Metropolitan Police deputy assistant commissioner Stephen Kavanagh confirmed that police in London were considering using baton rounds against rioters, not previously used by mainland police in public order operations (though they were first approved for use in England and Wales in 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">Metropolitan Police Service</a> has assigned 450 detectives to hunt for rioters and looters.<sup id="cite_ref-laville-looting_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laville-looting-225">[225]</a></sup> The list of photographed looters has been made available on their website.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Assistant Chief Constable Garry Shewan of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Police" title="Greater Manchester Police">Greater Manchester Police</a> criticised "unprecedented" criminality. On 10 August, he warned: "Hundreds and hundreds of people, we have your image, we have your face, we have your acts of wanton criminality on film."<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Research_in_Motion" class="mw-redirect" title="Research in Motion">Research in Motion</a> (RIM), the maker of the BlackBerry, are reported to have contacted the police to offer help in investigating the use of their system for the organisation of riots.<sup id="cite_ref-G8AUG2011_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G8AUG2011-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <i>The Independent</i>, the costs to the Metropolitan Police of policing the disorder and disturbances in London are expected to exceed £34 million. This could be more than their total bill for the policing of all major public disorder events in the year from April 2010 to March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-I30AUG2011_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I30AUG2011-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrests_and_charges">Arrests and charges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Arrests and charges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>By 15 August 2011 around 3,100 people had been arrested, of whom over 1,100 had appeared in court.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc15Aug_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc15Aug-13">[13]</a></sup> On 25 August the BBC reported that more than 2,000 people had been arrested in connection with the disorder in London.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC25AUG2011_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC25AUG2011-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice_system">Justice system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Justice system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sentencing_guidelines">Sentencing guidelines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sentencing guidelines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It was reported in mid-August that some courts were advised by senior justice clerks to deal harshly with offences committed during the disturbances.<sup id="cite_ref-dt_penalties_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt_penalties-230">[230]</a></sup> The advice was said to tell the courts that they could ignore existing sentencing guidelines and hand down heavy sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-dt_penalties_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt_penalties-230">[230]</a></sup> David Cameron defended the courts for handing out tough sentences, while some Liberal Democrat MPs and civil rights groups criticised some sentences being handed down.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Groups of lawyers complained that Crown Prosecutors were opposing bail in more cases than usual.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trials_and_sentencing">Trials and sentencing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Trials and sentencing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 1 September 2011 the BBC reported that official <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Justice (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Justice</a> figures showed that of the 1,566 people that had appeared before magistrates on charges connected with the disorder, 1,027 had been in London, 190 in Greater Manchester, 132 in the West Midlands, 67 in Merseyside and 64 in Nottingham.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1SEP2011_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1SEP2011-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sentences of four years in a <a href="/wiki/Young_Offender_Institution" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Offender Institution">Young Offender Institution</a> were given to two men who promoted riots via Facebook. The proposed events in <a href="/wiki/Northwich" title="Northwich">Northwich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a> were not attended by any other people.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_four_years_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_four_years-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sydney_morning_herald_four_years_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sydney_morning_herald_four_years-237">[237]</a></sup> These sentences were affirmed on appeal by the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales#Criminal_Division" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">Court of Appeal</a>. Giving the judgment of the court, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chief_Justice_of_England_and_Wales" title="Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales">Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Igor_Judge,_Baron_Judge" title="Igor Judge, Baron Judge">Lord Judge</a>, sitting with Sir John Thomas and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Leveson" title="Brian Leveson">Lord Justice Leveson</a>, stated that there is "an overwhelming obligation on sentencing courts to do what they can to ensure the protection of the public", that "the imposition of severe sentences, intended to provide both punishment and deterrence, must follow" and that "[t]hose who deliberately participate in disturbances of this magnitude, causing injury and damage and fear to even the most stout-hearted of citizens, and who individually commit further crimes during the course of the riots are committing aggravated crimes". The appeals were dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 April 2012, the Court of Appeal (Lord Judge CJ, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Openshaw" title="Peter Openshaw">Openshaw</a> &amp; Irwin <a href="/wiki/High_Court_judge" class="mw-redirect" title="High Court judge">JJ</a>) increased the sentence imposed by the Crown Court at Inner London on Adam Ahmadzai from four years detention to seven years detention for offences of violent disorder, robbery, burglary and criminal damage committed during the riots on 8 August 2011, after a reference from <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Attorney General of England and Wales">Attorney General</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Grieve" title="Dominic Grieve">Dominic Grieve</a> <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Counsel" title="Queen's Counsel">QC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> The Lord Chief Justice stated that the offences were of the "greatest possible seriousness".<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></p>
<p>A woman who had not taken part in the riots received five months for receiving a pair of stolen shorts. The sentence was later reduced on appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> Manchester police used Twitter to celebrate the five-month sentence; they later apologised and removed the tweet.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> A teenager was freed when prosecutors found evidence he had been wrongly charged with arson. While in prison, his own flat was burned down.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> The detaining of under-18s without <a href="/wiki/Criminal_record" title="Criminal record">criminal records</a> was criticised by <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> in October 2011 for possibly breaching the 1989 UN <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_unicef_criticises_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_unicef_criticises-245">[245]</a></sup> By August 2012, 1292 rioters had been handed custodial sentences totalling 1,800 years at 16.8 months on an average.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical">Theatrical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Theatrical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tricycle_Theatre" title="Tricycle Theatre">The Tricycle Theatre</a> in Kilburn presented a piece of new writing, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Riots_(2011_play)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Riots (2011 play)">The Riots</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Gillian_Slovo" title="Gillian Slovo">Gillian Slovo</a>, which looked into the events over those days in August and the thoughts and opinions of a range of people directly involved and politicians. It transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Grant_Arts_Centre" title="Bernie Grant Arts Centre">Bernie Grant Arts Centre</a> in Tottenham, about 400m from where the Mark Duggan protest took place, on 5 January 2012, and is due to run until 15 January. The piece attempts to show a non-biased look into the events, allowing audience members to hear different views into why it happened and what could have and should now be done. The piece includes community leaders Stafford Scott and Martin Sylvester Brown, police constables on duty that night and a former resident of the Carpet-Right building, the burned remains now providing a highly poignant reminder of the events. They are combined with the views of <a href="/wiki/Diane_Abbott" title="Diane Abbott">Diane Abbott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iain_Duncan_Smith" title="Iain Duncan Smith">Iain Duncan Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gove" title="Michael Gove">Michael Gove</a> and Pastor Nims Obunge. It was received well by all critics, with 4 stars from all major press including <i>The Guardian</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_description">Alternative description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Alternative description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While authorities and mass media referred to these events as <a href="/wiki/Riots" class="mw-redirect" title="Riots">riots</a>, sympathisers described them as protest,<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Insurrection" class="mw-redirect" title="Insurrection">insurrection</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DN10Aug_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN10Aug-250">[250]</a></sup> or "English Spring"<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> (to parallel the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Suggested_contributory_factors">Suggested contributory factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Suggested contributory factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The causes of the 2011 England riots both immediate and long-term have been the subject of media and academic debate. Several speculations have emerged as to what the likely contributory factors might be for the riots; from <a href="/wiki/Socio-economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economic">socio-economic</a> causes focusing on unemployment and spending cuts, as well as <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gang_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Gang culture">gang culture</a> and criminal opportunism. The House of Commons Home Affairs select committee will begin examining the police response to the riots in late 2011. The <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">leader of the Opposition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Miliband" title="Ed Miliband">Ed Miliband</a>, called for a public inquiry into the wider causes of the riots and has stated that his party would set up such an inquiry if the coalition fails to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> The UK was shaken by worst riots in decades.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>A wide-ranging <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">LSE</a> study called <i>Reading the Riots</i> concluded that the major contributory factors were opportunism, perceived social injustice, deprivation, and frustration at the way communities were policed.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a> poll was carried out on 8–9 August 2011 for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> asking what those surveyed believed to be the main cause of the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> In it, 42% of those polled thought "criminal behaviour" to be the main cause, whilst 26% thought "gang culture" was, 8% thought "government cuts" were, 5% thought "unemployment" was, 5% thought "racial tensions" was and 3% thought "poor policing" was. In a <a href="/wiki/ComRes" title="ComRes">ComRes</a> poll for the <i>Sunday Mirror</i> and <i>Independent on Sunday</i>, in which the question was "do you agree or disagree with these statements about the recent riots?", 90% of those polled agreed that the "Police should be allowed use [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] to water cannon to disperse rioters", 90% agreed that "There is no excuse whatsoever for the violent rioting and looting over the last few days", 61% agreed that "Government ministers failed to return to their desks quickly enough from holidays" and 50% agreed that "The Government's response to the economic crisis (e.g. cuts to services, unemployment, reduced education funding) is helping fuel the rioters".<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p>Researchers who study the causes of political instability suggest that the critical common factor is the density of youths. A nation's extent of political unrest, i.e. its vulnerability to riot, war or regime change, is directly associated with the percentage of 15- to 24-year-olds in its population. They argue that communities with more than 20% of individuals in this age group run the greatest risk of more frequent and more intense political instability. They describe the phenomena as the "<a href="/wiki/Youth_bulge" class="mw-redirect" title="Youth bulge">youth bulge theory</a>", where the "bulge" refers to the fattening of the population pyramid just before the base of the youngest age groups.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poor_relations_with_police">Poor relations with police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Poor relations with police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The riots in Tottenham after the death of Mark Duggan were initially blamed on poor relations between the police and the black community.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> Professor <a href="/wiki/Gus_John" title="Gus John">Gus John</a> has argued that the tactical use of frequent "<a href="/wiki/Stop_and_search" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop and search">stop and search</a>", particularly of young black men, has caused resentment of the police in the black community.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a>, the MP for Tottenham, the "cracks that already existed between the police and the community became deep fissures".<sup id="cite_ref-lammy_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lammy-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-polcl_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polcl-261">[261]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Guardian</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Reading the Riots Survey concluded: "Although rioters expressed a mix of opinions about the disorder, many of those involved said they felt like they were participating in explicitly anti-police riots. They cited "policing" as the most significant cause of the riots, and anger over the police shooting of Mark Duggan, which triggered initial disturbances in Tottenham, was repeatedly mentioned – even outside London."<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_exclusion">Social exclusion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Social exclusion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rioters themselves cited exclusion as a reason for their actions. One person, asked by a journalist if rioting was really the best way to accomplish their objectives, responded: "Yes, because if we weren’t rioting, you wouldn’t be talking to us."<sup id="cite_ref-DN10Aug_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN10Aug-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Camila_Batmanghelidjh" title="Camila Batmanghelidjh">Camila Batmanghelidjh</a> writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> blames <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_deprivation" title="Social deprivation">social deprivation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> Various journalists have identified poverty and the <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">growing gap between rich and poor</a> as causative factors.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a House of Commons debate on the riots Home Secretary <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> stated that the riots were symptomatic of a "wider malaise" including worklessness, illiteracy, and drug abuse but also stated that "Everybody, no matter what their background or circumstances, has the freedom to choose between right and wrong".<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, writing in <i>The Observer</i>, stated that the riots were not caused by a broken society, but due to a group of young, alienated, disaffected youth who are outside the social mainstream and who live in a culture at odds with any canons of proper behaviour; he added that this is found in virtually every developed nation.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Max_Hastings" title="Max Hastings">Max Hastings</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> blamed a culture of welfare dependence.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup></p>
<p>A journalist on Al Jazeera suggested a similarity to the disenfranchisement behind the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_wave" title="Revolutionary wave">revolutionary wave</a> of 2011. Links were made to high youth unemployment and general disenfranchisement.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> A study by The <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> published in September 2011 found a strong link between rioting and deprivation.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_breakdown">Family breakdown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Family breakdown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Christina Odone writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> links the riots to a lack of male role models and argues that "Like the overwhelming majority of youth offenders behind bars, these gang members have one thing in common: no father at home."<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> This has been linked further with England's having the "worst record in family breakdown in Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_cuts">Government cuts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Government cuts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The spending cuts of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_coalition_government_(2010%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom coalition government (2010–present)">coalition government in the United Kingdom</a> have also been cited as a cause.<sup id="cite_ref-polcl_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polcl-261">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dlammy_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dlammy-277">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> Ken Livingstone, the Labour Candidate for Mayor of London in 2012 has argued that "The economic stagnation and cuts being imposed by the Tory government inevitably create social division."<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> Nick Clegg, the <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy Prime Minister</a> and leader of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats" title="Liberal Democrats">Liberal Democrats political party</a>, made it clear that the government's planned cuts to police budgets will go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
<p>The local government budget had been cut in the past year so Haringey Council, which includes <a href="/wiki/Tottenham" title="Tottenham">Tottenham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hale" title="Tottenham Hale">Tottenham Hale</a>, decided to close eight of its 13 youth clubs in 2011, rather than save money through increased efficiency or make cuts in other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scrapping of the <a href="/wiki/Education_Maintenance_Allowance" title="Education Maintenance Allowance">Education Maintenance Allowance</a>, removing of funding for courses where the student already has an equal or lower level qualification and trebling of university tuition fees, combined with high youth unemployment has placed the British youth "between a rock and a hard place" alienating and angering the youth population.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> Proponents of this argument say that Scottish youth did not riot partly because Scottish students do not have to pay tuition fees.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unemployment_and_poverty">Unemployment and poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Unemployment and poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a> MP has said that Tottenham has the highest unemployment rate in London and the eighth highest in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> The number of people chasing every one job vacancy in Haringey has been put at 23 and 54 in separate reports, and fears had spread of disorder after youth club closures in recent months.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup></p>
<p>Low economic growth and highest unemployment rate in decades.<sup id="cite_ref-polcl_261-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polcl-261">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> Haringey, has the fourth highest level of child poverty in London and 8.8% unemployed.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rioting_for_fun">Rioting for fun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Rioting for fun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other academics have pointed to more prosaic causes of the 2011 riots, citing the <a href="/wiki/Carnivalesque" title="Carnivalesque">carnivalesque</a> atmospheres created through the usual uses of urban space. For example, researchers from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">University of Birmingham</a> noted that ‘another sound could be heard above the mêlée, that of laughter. Above the bark of police dogs, and behind the masked and hooded faces of the throng, were smiles, laughter, and shrieks of joy.’<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gang_culture">Gang culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Gang culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a <i><a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">Newsnight</a></i> discussion on 12 August, historian <a href="/wiki/David_Starkey" title="David Starkey">David Starkey</a> blamed black gangster culture, saying that it had influenced youths of all races.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-210">[210]</a></sup> The BBC received nearly 700 complaints about his statement that the "whites have become black".<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> Cottrell-Boyce, writing in the Youth Justice journal, argued that gangs were constructed as a 'suitable enemy' by politicians and the media, obscuring the wider, structural and economic roots of youth violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Cottrell-Boyce_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cottrell-Boyce-296">[296]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_opportunism">Criminal opportunism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Criminal opportunism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the riots, on 9 August 2011, UK Home Secretary <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> said: "I think this is about sheer criminality. That is what we have seen on the streets. The violence we've seen, the looting we've seen, the thuggery we've seen – this is sheer criminality, and let's make no bones about it."<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> Paul Hobbs, London correspondent for <a href="/wiki/One_News_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="One News (New Zealand)">One News</a> said that looters are not politically motivated and called the riots "recreational violence".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-298">[298]</a></sup> A Manchester rioter said to a BBC correspondent: "Every time I go into town I just think how the shops got smashed up in 2011 by all of us, I just laugh about it every time I go back in now."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>The BBC reported that the Chief Constable of West Midlands Police had stated that he thought that the motivation for rioters targeting the city centre was not anger, but greed.<sup id="cite_ref-greed_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greed-300">[300]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moral_decay_at_the_top">Moral decay at the top</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Moral decay at the top">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Daily Telegraph</i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Oborne" title="Peter Oborne">Peter Oborne</a> suggested that moral decay is just as bad at the top of society as it is at the bottom, with the rich and powerful generating anger among the British population. He cited the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_parliamentary_expenses_scandal" title="United Kingdom parliamentary expenses scandal">MPs' expenses scandal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bankers%27_bonuses" title="Bankers' bonuses">bankers' bonuses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/News_International_phone_hacking_scandal" title="News International phone hacking scandal">the phone hacking scandal</a> as setting poor examples.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Financial_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="The Financial Times">The Financial Times</a></i> cartoonist Ingram Pinn depicted a Union Flag being broken through by a looter in a <a href="/wiki/Hoodie" title="Hoodie">hoodie</a> carrying a stolen box of Adidas trainers, preceded by two men in suits carrying piles of cash, one saying "MP's Expenses" and another "Banker's Bonus".<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Failure_of_the_penal_system">Failure of the penal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Failure of the penal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Clarke" title="Kenneth Clarke">Kenneth Clarke</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Justice" title="Secretary of State for Justice">Secretary of State for Justice</a>, writing in <i>The Guardian</i>, described the riots in part as "an outburst of outrageous behaviour by the criminal classes". He drew attention to the statistic that almost three-quarters of the adults who had been charged with offences related to the disorder already had a criminal record. Clarke characterised this as the legacy of "a broken penal system", one that did not have a good record for preventing reoffending. He stated he is proposing radical new measures intended to focus on robust punishment and on delivering reductions in reoffending.<sup id="cite_ref-G5SEP2011_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G5SEP2011-303">[303]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainstream_media_relationship_with_the_communities">Mainstream media relationship with the communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Mainstream media relationship with the communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A conference held in November 2012 and its subsequent report by Dr Leah Bassel of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leicester" title="University of Leicester">University of Leicester</a>, entitled <i>Media and the Riots – A Call For Action</i>, examined the relationship between mainstream media and communities affected by the riots.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (October 2013)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (October 2013)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Celebrity_involvement">Celebrity involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Celebrity involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jamie_Waylett" title="Jamie Waylett">Jamie Waylett</a>, who played Vincent Crabbe in the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">Harry Potter</a></i> film series, was charged and sentenced for his participation in the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-307">[307]</a></sup> He was photographed drinking out of a bottle of stolen champagne as well as holding a petrol bomb in Camden on the third day of rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_307-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-307">[307]</a></sup> He was given a two-year sentence for violence and handling stolen goods.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_307-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-307">[307]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_England_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dl>
<dd><span class="reference-text">"There has been much speculation about the causes and meanings of the riots that swept through English cities in August 2011...</span>
<p><span class="reference-text">"These disturbances began on 6 August following the police shooting of Mark Duggan, a black resident of Tottenham, North London. Over the following days, they spread within London and to other English cities....</span></p>
<p><span class="reference-text">"There were no riots in English cities such as Sheffield and Newcastle, and the streets of Welsh and Scottish cities remained equally calm."</span></p>
